## Section 3: Data File Schemas

### 1. users.txt
- Fields: `username|email|fullname|created_date`
- Description:
  - username: string, unique identifier for user
  - email: string, user's email address
  - fullname: string, user's full name
  - created_date: date in YYYY-MM-DD format
- Example:
  ```
  john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15
  alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16
  bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17
  admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10
  ```

### 2. articles.txt
- Fields: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date`
- Description:
  - article_id: int, unique article identifier
  - title: string
  - author: string (username)
  - category: string enum (news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release)
  - status: string enum (draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived)
  - tags: comma-separated string list
  - featured_image: string URL or empty
  - meta_description: string
  - created_date: date YYYY-MM-DD
  - publish_date: datetime YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS or empty if unpublished
- Example:
  ```
  1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00
  2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00
  3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|
  ```

### 3. article_versions.txt
- Fields: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary`
- Description:
  - version_id: int unique version identifier
  - article_id: int foreign key linking to articles.txt
  - version_number: int (incrementing per article)
  - content: string (full article content text)
  - author: string (username who edited)
  - created_date: datetime YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS
  - change_summary: string describing version changes
- Example:
  ```
  1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft
  2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction
  3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version
  ```

### 4. approvals.txt
- Fields: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp`
- Description:
  - approval_id: int unique approval record
  - article_id: int
  - version_id: int
  - approver: string (username)
  - status: string enum (approved, rejected, revision_requested)
  - comments: string
  - timestamp: datetime YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS
- Example:
  ```
  1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00
  2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00
  3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00
  ```

### 5. workflow_stages.txt
- Fields: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required`
- Description:
  - stage_id: int unique
  - category: string (article category)
  - stage_name: string
  - stage_order: int (order of workflow stage)
  - is_required: string enum ('yes', 'no')
- Example:
  ```
  1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes
  2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes
  3|news|Editor Review|1|yes
  4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes
  5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes
  ```

### 6. comments.txt
- Fields: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp`
- Description:
  - comment_id: int unique
  - article_id: int
  - version_id: int
  - user: string (username who commented)
  - comment_text: string
  - timestamp: datetime YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS
- Example:
  ```
  1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00
  2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00
  3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00
  ```

### 7. analytics.txt
- Fields: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares`
- Description:
  - analytics_id: int unique
  - article_id: int
  - date: date YYYY-MM-DD
  - views: int number of views
  - unique_visitors: int
  - avg_time_seconds: int average time on page
  - shares: int number of shares
- Example:
  ```
  1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12
  2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18
  3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15
  4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8
  ```

---

This specification document provides clear definitions for routes, template elements, and data file formats enabling separation of backend and frontend development for the ContentPublishingHub application.

=== architecture.md ===
# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document

---

## Section 1: Backend System Design

### 1.1 Flask Application Structure

The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:

```
/content_publishing_hub
  /app
    /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area
    /services          # Business logic and processing services
    /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions
    /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)
    /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic
    /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed
    /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)
    __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints
  /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)
  config.py            # Configuration settings
  run.py               # Application entry point
  requirements.txt     # Python dependencies
```

### 1.2 Module Responsibilities

- **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.

- **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.

- **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.

- **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.

- **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.

- **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.

### 1.3 Data File Access and Management

- All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory.
- The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data.
- Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption.
- Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications.
- Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.

### 1.4 Data Flow

- User requests hit Flask routes (controllers).
- Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods.
- Service methods utilize models to load and update data files.
- Version control service manages version and approval related workflows.
- Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering.
- For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files.
- For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.

---

## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints

| Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes |
|-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------|
| /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard
| /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history
| /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status
| /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles
| /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary

### Routing Details

- Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed.
- GET routes primarily fetch and display data.
- POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions.
- Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering.
- Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.

---

## Section 3: Version Control Design

### 3.1 Architecture Overview

- Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID.
- Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary.
- Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps.
- Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion.
- Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.

### 3.2 Data Relationships

- `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`.
- `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version.
- `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback.
- `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.

### 3.3 Versioning Workflow

- When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number.
- Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow.
- Comments can be added during review for each version.
- Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary.
- Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.

### 3.4 Storage and Access

- Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions.
- Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.

---

## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points

### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates

- Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications.
- Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values.
- Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.

### 4.2 Endpoint Responses

- GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data.
- POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.

### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend

- Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs.
- Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering.
- Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.

---

This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.

  [architecture.md] # ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document  ---  ## Section 1: Backend System Design  ### 1.1 Flask Application Structure  The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:  ``` /content_publishing_hub   /app     /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area     /services          # Business logic and processing services     /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions     /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)     /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic     /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed     /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)     __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints   /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)   config.py            # Configuration settings   run.py               # Application entry point   requirements.txt     # Python dependencies ```  ### 1.2 Module Responsibilities  - **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.  - **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.  - **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.  - **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.  - **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.  - **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.  ### 1.3 Data File Access and Management  - All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory. - The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data. - Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption. - Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications. - Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.  ### 1.4 Data Flow  - User requests hit Flask routes (controllers). - Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods. - Service methods utilize models to load and update data files. - Version control service manages version and approval related workflows. - Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering. - For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files. - For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.  ---  ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints  | Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes | |-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------| | /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard | /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history | /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status | /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles | /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary  ### Routing Details  - Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed. - GET routes primarily fetch and display data. - POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions. - Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering. - Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.  ---  ## Section 3: Version Control Design  ### 3.1 Architecture Overview  - Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID. - Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary. - Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps. - Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion. - Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.  ### 3.2 Data Relationships  - `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`. - `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version. - `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback. - `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.  ### 3.3 Versioning Workflow  - When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number. - Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow. - Comments can be added during review for each version. - Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary. - Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.  ### 3.4 Storage and Access  - Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions. - Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.  ---  ## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points  ### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates  - Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications. - Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values. - Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.  ### 4.2 Endpoint Responses  - GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data. - POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.  ### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend  - Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs. - Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering. - Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.  ---  This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.

Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.  - **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.  - **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.  - **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.  - **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.  - **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.  ### 1.3 Data File Access and Management  - All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory. - The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data. - Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption. - Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications. - Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.  ### 1.4 Data Flow  - User requests hit Flask routes (controllers). - Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods. - Service methods utilize models to load and update data files. - Version control service manages version and approval related workflows. - Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering. - For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files. - For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.  ---  ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints  | Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes | |-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------| | /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard | /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history | /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status | /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles | /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary  ### Routing Details  - For session management\n\n# Paths to data files in /data directory\nDATA_DIR = './data'\nARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'article_versions.txt')\nAPPROVALS_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'approvals.txt')\n\n# Utility functions for file IO and data parsing\n\ndef read_article_versions():\n    articles = {}\n    if not os.path.exists(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE):\n        return articles\n    with open(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE, 'r') as f:\n        lines = f.readlines()\n        for line in lines:\n            parts = line.strip().split('|')\n            # Expect line format: article_id|version_num|timestamp|summary|content\n            if len(parts) < 5:\n                continue\n            article_id, version, timestamp, summary, content = parts\n            if article_id not in articles:\n                articles[article_id] = []\n            articles[article_id].append({\n                'version': int(version),\n                'timestamp': timestamp,\n                'summary': summary,\n                'content': content\n            })\n    return articles\n\ndef save_article_versions(articles):\n    with open(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE, 'w') as f:\n        for article_id, versions in articles.items():\n            for v in versions:\n                line = f\"{article_id}|{v['version']}|{v['timestamp']}|{v['summary']}|{v['content']}\\n\"\n                f.write(line)\n\ndef read_approvals():\n    approvals = {}\n    if not os.path.exists(APPROVALS_FILE):\n        return approvals\n    with open(APPROVALS_FILE, 'r') as f:\n        lines = f.readlines()\n        for line in lines:\n            # Expected line format: article_id|version|approver|status|comments\n            parts = line.strip().split('|')\n            if len(parts) < 5:\n                continue\n            article_id, version, approver, status, comments = parts\n            key = (article_id, int(version))\n            if key not in approvals:\n                approvals[key] = []\n            approvals[key].append({\n                'approver': approver,\n                'status': status,\n                'comments': comments\n            })\n    return approvals\n\ndef save_approvals(approvals):\n    with open(APPROVALS_FILE, 'w') as f:\n        for (article_id, version), approval_list in approvals.items():\n            for a in approval_list:\n                line = f\"{article_id}|{version}|{a['approver']}|{a['status']}|{a['comments']}\\n\"\n                f.write(line)\n\n# Route: Create article POST\n@app.route('/article/create', methods=['GET', 'POST'])\ndef create_article():\n    if request.method == 'POST':\n        article_id = request.form.get('article_id', '').strip()\n        summary = request.form.get('summary', '').strip()\n        content = request.form.get('content', '').strip()\n\n        if not article_id or not content:\n            flash('Article ID and content are required')\n            return render_template('create_article.html')\n\n        articles = read_article_versions()\n        if article_id in articles:\n            flash('Article ID already exists. Use edit to add versions.')\n            return render_template('create_article.html')\n\n        timestamp = datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()\n        new_version = {\n            'version': 1,\n            'timestamp': timestamp,\n            'summary': summary,\n            'content': content\n        }\n        articles[article_id] = [new_version]\n        save_article_versions(articles)\n        flash('Article created successfully')\n        return redirect(url_for('edit_article', article_id=article_id))\n\n    return render_template('create_article.html')\n\n# Route: Edit article GET+POST\n@app.route('/article/<article_id>/edit', methods=['GET', 'POST'])\ndef edit_article(article_id):\n    articles = read_article_versions()\n    if article_id not in articles:\n        flash('Article not found')\n        return redirect(url_for('create_article'))\n\n    if request.method == 'POST':\n        summary = request.form.get('summary', '').strip()\n        content = request.form.get('content', '').strip()\n        if not content:\n            flash('Content cannot be empty')\n            return render_template('edit_article.html', article_id=article_id, latest_version=articles[article_id][-1])\n\n        # Create new version\n        last_version_num = articles[article_id][-1]['version']\n        new_version_num = last_version_num + 1\n        timestamp = datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()\n        new_version = {\n            'version': new_version_num,\n            'timestamp': timestamp,\n            'summary': summary,\n            'content': content\n        }\n        articles[article_id].append(new_version)\n        save_article_versions(articles)\n        flash('Article updated with new version')\n\n        return redirect(url_for('view_article_versions', article_id=article_id))\n\n    latest_version = articles[article_id][-1]\n    return render_template('edit_article.html', article_id=article_id, latest_version=latest_version)\n\n# Route: View article versions\n@app.route('/article/<article_id>/versions')\ndef view_article_versions(article_id):\n    articles = read_article_versions()\n    if article_id not in articles:\n        flash('Article not found')\n        return redirect(url_for('create_article'))\n\n    versions = articles[article_id]\n    approvals = read_approvals()\n    # Prepare approvals for this article versions\n    version_approvals = {}\n    for v in versions:\n        key = (article_id, v['version'])\n        version_approvals[v['version']] = approvals.get(key, [])\n\n    return render_template('article_versions.html', article_id=article_id, versions=versions, approvals=version_approvals)\n\n# Route: Approve a version (POST) to update approval status\n@app.route('/article/<article_id>/approve', methods=['POST'])\ndef approve_article(article_id):\n    version_num = int(request.form.get('version', '0'))\n    approver = request.form.get('approver', '').strip()\n    status = request.form.get('status', '').strip()  # e.g. Approved, Rejected, Pending\n    comments = request.form.get('comments', '').strip()\n\n    if not approver or not status or version_num < 1:\n        flash('Missing approval data')\n        return redirect(url_for('view_article_versions', article_id=article_id))\n\n    approvals = read_approvals()\n    key = (article_id, version_num)\n    if key not in approvals:\n        approvals[key] = []\n\n    # Add approval record\n    approvals[key].append({\n        'approver': approver,\n        'status': status,\n        'comments': comments\n    })\n    save_approvals(approvals)\n    flash('Approval status updated')\n\n    return redirect(url_for('view_article_versions', article_id=article_id))\n\n# Route: Analytics for article\n@app.route('/analytics/<article_id>')\ndef analytics(article_id):\n    # For demonstration, collect simple stats\n    articles = read_article_versions()\n    if article_id not in articles:\n        flash('Article not found')\n        return redirect(url_for('create_article'))\n\n    versions = articles[article_id]\n    total_versions = len(versions)\n\n    # Some fake stats for this example\n    analytics_data = {\n        'article_id': article_id,\n        'total_versions': total_versions,\n        'unique_approvers': set(),\n        'approval_counts': {}\n    }\n\n    approvals = read_approvals()\n    for v in versions:\n        key = (article_id, v['version'])\n        version_approvals = approvals.get(key, [])\n        for ap in version_approvals:\n            analytics_data['unique_approvers'].add(ap['approver'])\n            analytics_data['approval_counts'][ap['status']] = analytics_data['approval_counts'].get(ap['status'], 0) + 1\n\n    analytics_data['unique_approvers_count'] = len(analytics_data['unique_approvers'])\n\n    return render_template('analytics.html', analytics=analytics_data)\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    app.run(debug=True)\n"})

=== LLM_call: SystemArchitect ===
INPUT: === architecture.md ===
# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document

---

## Section 1: Backend System Design

### 1.1 Flask Application Structure

The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:

```
/content_publishing_hub
  /app
    /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area
    /services          # Business logic and processing services
    /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions
    /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)
    /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic
    /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed
    /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)
    __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints
  /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)
  config.py            # Configuration settings
  run.py               # Application entry point
  requirements.txt     # Python dependencies
```

### 1.2 Module Responsibilities

- **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.

- **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.

- **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.

- **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.

- **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.

- **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.

### 1.3 Data File Access and Management

- All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory.
- The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data.
- Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption.
- Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications.
- Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.

### 1.4 Data Flow

- User requests hit Flask routes (controllers).
- Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods.
- Service methods utilize models to load and update data files.
- Version control service manages version and approval related workflows.
- Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering.
- For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files.
- For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.

---

## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints

| Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes |
|-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------|
| /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard
| /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history
| /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status
| /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles
| /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary

### Routing Details

- Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed.
- GET routes primarily fetch and display data.
- POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions.
- Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering.
- Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.

---

## Section 3: Version Control Design

### 3.1 Architecture Overview

- Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID.
- Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary.
- Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps.
- Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion.
- Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.

### 3.2 Data Relationships

- `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`.
- `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version.
- `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback.
- `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.

### 3.3 Versioning Workflow

- When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number.
- Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow.
- Comments can be added during review for each version.
- Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary.
- Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.

### 3.4 Storage and Access

- Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions.
- Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.

---

## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points

### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates

- Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications.
- Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values.
- Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.

### 4.2 Endpoint Responses

- GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data.
- POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.

### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend

- Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs.
- Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering.
- Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.

---

This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.


=== app.py ===
from flask import Flask, request, render_template, redirect, url_for, session, flash
import os
import datetime

app = Flask(__name__)
app.secret_key = 'supersecretkey'  # For session management

# Paths to data files in /data directory
DATA_DIR = './data'
ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'article_versions.txt')
APPROVALS_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'approvals.txt')

# Utility functions for file IO and data parsing

def read_article_versions():
    articles = {}
    if not os.path.exists(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE):
        return articles
    with open(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE, 'r') as f:
        lines = f.readlines()
        for line in lines:
            parts = line.strip().split('|')
            # Expect line format: article_id|version_num|timestamp|summary|content
            if len(parts) < 5:
                continue
            article_id, version, timestamp, summary, content = parts
            if article_id not in articles:
                articles[article_id] = []
            articles[article_id].append({
                'version': int(version),
                'timestamp': timestamp,
                'summary': summary,
                'content': content
            })
    return articles

def save_article_versions(articles):
    with open(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE, 'w') as f:
        for article_id, versions in articles.items():
            for v in versions:
                line = f"{article_id}|{v['version']}|{v['timestamp']}|{v['summary']}|{v['content']}\n"
                f.write(line)

def read_approvals():
    approvals = {}
    if not os.path.exists(APPROVALS_FILE):
        return approvals
    with open(APPROVALS_FILE, 'r') as f:
        lines = f.readlines()
        for line in lines:
            # Expected line format: article_id|version|approver|status|comments
            parts = line.strip().split('|')
            if len(parts) < 5:
                continue
            article_id, version, approver, status, comments = parts
            key = (article_id, int(version))
            if key not in approvals:
                approvals[key] = []
            approvals[key].append({
                'approver': approver,
                'status': status,
                'comments': comments
            })
    return approvals

def save_approvals(approvals):
    with open(APPROVALS_FILE, 'w') as f:
        for (article_id, version), approval_list in approvals.items():
            for a in approval_list:
                line = f"{article_id}|{version}|{a['approver']}|{a['status']}|{a['comments']}\n"
                f.write(line)

# Route: Create article POST
@app.route('/article/create', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
def create_article():
    if request.method == 'POST':
        article_id = request.form.get('article_id', '').strip()
        summary = request.form.get('summary', '').strip()
        content = request.form.get('content', '').strip()

        if not article_id or not content:
            flash('Article ID and content are required')
            return render_template('create_article.html')

        articles = read_article_versions()
        if article_id in articles:
            flash('Article ID already exists. Use edit to add versions.')
            return render_template('create_article.html')

        timestamp = datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()
        new_version = {
            'version': 1,
            'timestamp': timestamp,
            'summary': summary,
            'content': content
        }
        articles[article_id] = [new_version]
        save_article_versions(articles)
        flash('Article created successfully')
        return redirect(url_for('edit_article', article_id=article_id))

    return render_template('create_article.html')

# Route: Edit article GET+POST
@app.route('/article/<article_id>/edit', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
def edit_article(article_id):
    articles = read_article_versions()
    if article_id not in articles:
        flash('Article not found')
        return redirect(url_for('create_article'))

    if request.method == 'POST':
        summary = request.form.get('summary', '').strip()
        content = request.form.get('content', '').strip()
        if not content:
            flash('Content cannot be empty')
            return render_template('edit_article.html', article_id=article_id, latest_version=articles[article_id][-1])

        # Create new version
        last_version_num = articles[article_id][-1]['version']
        new_version_num = last_version_num + 1
        timestamp = datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()
        new_version = {
            'version': new_version_num,
            'timestamp': timestamp,
            'summary': summary,
            'content': content
        }
        articles[article_id].append(new_version)
        save_article_versions(articles)
        flash('Article updated with new version')

        return redirect(url_for('view_article_versions', article_id=article_id))

    latest_version = articles[article_id][-1]
    return render_template('edit_article.html', article_id=article_id, latest_version=latest_version)

# Route: View article versions
@app.route('/article/<article_id>/versions')
def view_article_versions(article_id):
    articles = read_article_versions()
    if article_id not in articles:
        flash('Article not found')
        return redirect(url_for('create_article'))

    versions = articles[article_id]
    approvals = read_approvals()
    # Prepare approvals for this article versions
    version_approvals = {}
    for v in versions:
        key = (article_id, v['version'])
        version_approvals[v['version']] = approvals.get(key, [])

    return render_template('article_versions.html', article_id=article_id, versions=versions, approvals=version_approvals)

# Route: Approve a version (POST) to update approval status
@app.route('/article/<article_id>/approve', methods=['POST'])
def approve_article(article_id):
    version_num = int(request.form.get('version', '0'))
    approver = request.form.get('approver', '').strip()
    status = request.form.get('status', '').strip()  # e.g. Approved, Rejected, Pending
    comments = request.form.get('comments', '').strip()

    if not approver or not status or version_num < 1:
        flash('Missing approval data')
        return redirect(url_for('view_article_versions', article_id=article_id))

    approvals = read_approvals()
    key = (article_id, version_num)
    if key not in approvals:
        approvals[key] = []

    # Add approval record
    approvals[key].append({
        'approver': approver,
        'status': status,
        'comments': comments
    })
    save_approvals(approvals)
    flash('Approval status updated')

    return redirect(url_for('view_article_versions', article_id=article_id))

# Route: Analytics for article
@app.route('/analytics/<article_id>')
def analytics(article_id):
    # For demonstration, collect simple stats
    articles = read_article_versions()
    if article_id not in articles:
        flash('Article not found')
        return redirect(url_for('create_article'))

    versions = articles[article_id]
    total_versions = len(versions)

    # Some fake stats for this example
    analytics_data = {
        'article_id': article_id,
        'total_versions': total_versions,
        'unique_approvers': set(),
        'approval_counts': {}
    }

    approvals = read_approvals()
    for v in versions:
        key = (article_id, v['version'])
        version_approvals = approvals.get(key, [])
        for ap in version_approvals:
            analytics_data['unique_approvers'].add(ap['approver'])
            analytics_data['approval_counts'][ap['status']] = analytics_data['approval_counts'].get(ap['status'], 0) + 1

    analytics_data['unique_approvers_count'] = len(analytics_data['unique_approvers'])

    return render_template('analytics.html', analytics=analytics_data)


if __name__ == '__main__':
    app.run(debug=True)

  [architecture.md] # ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document  ---  ## Section 1: Backend System Design  ### 1.1 Flask Application Structure  The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:  ``` /content_publishing_hub   /app     /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area     /services          # Business logic and processing services     /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions     /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)     /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic     /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed     /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)     __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints   /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)   config.py            # Configuration settings   run.py               # Application entry point   requirements.txt     # Python dependencies ```  ### 1.2 Module Responsibilities  - **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.  - **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.  - **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.  - **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.  - **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.  - **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.  ### 1.3 Data File Access and Management  - All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory. - The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data. - Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption. - Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications. - Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.  ### 1.4 Data Flow  - User requests hit Flask routes (controllers). - Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods. - Service methods utilize models to load and update data files. - Version control service manages version and approval related workflows. - Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering. - For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files. - For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.  ---  ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints  | Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes | |-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------| | /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard | /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history | /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status | /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles | /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary  ### Routing Details  - Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed. - GET routes primarily fetch and display data. - POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions. - Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering. - Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.  ---  ## Section 3: Version Control Design  ### 3.1 Architecture Overview  - Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID. - Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary. - Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps. - Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion. - Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.  ### 3.2 Data Relationships  - `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`. - `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version. - `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback. - `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.  ### 3.3 Versioning Workflow  - When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number. - Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow. - Comments can be added during review for each version. - Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary. - Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.  ### 3.4 Storage and Access  - Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions. - Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.  ---  ## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points  ### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates  - Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications. - Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values. - Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.  ### 4.2 Endpoint Responses  - GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data. - POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.  ### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend  - Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs. - Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering. - Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.  ---  This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.

# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document

---

## Section 1: Backend System Design

### 1.1 Flask Application Structure

The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:

```
/content_publishing_hub
  /app
    /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area
    /services          # Business logic and processing services
    /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions
    /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)
    /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic
    /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed
    /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)
    __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints
  /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)
  config.py            # Configuration settings
  run.py               # Application entry point
  requirements.txt     # Python dependencies
```

### 1.2 Module Responsibilities

- **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.

- **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.

- **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.

- **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.

- **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.

- **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.

### 1.3 Data File Access and Management

- All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory.
- The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data.
- Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption.
- Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications.
- Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.

### 1.4 Data Flow

- User requests hit Flask routes (controllers).
- Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods.
- Service methods utilize models to load and update data files.
- Version control service manages version and approval related workflows.
- Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering.
- For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files.
- For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.

---

## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints

| Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes |
|-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------|
| /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard
| /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history
| /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status
| /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles
| /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary

### Routing Details

- Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed.
- GET routes primarily fetch and display data.
- POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions.
- Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering.
- Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.

---

## Section 3: Version Control Design

### 3.1 Architecture Overview

- Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID.
- Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary.
- Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps.
- Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion.
- Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.

### 3.2 Data Relationships

- `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`.
- `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version.
- `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback.
- `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.

### 3.3 Versioning Workflow

- When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number.
- Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow.
- Comments can be added during review for each version.
- Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary.
- Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.

### 3.4 Storage and Access

- Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions.
- Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.

---

## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points

### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates

- Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications.
- Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values.
- Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.

### 4.2 Endpoint Responses

- GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data.
- POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.

### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend

- Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs.
- Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering.
- Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.

---

This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.

[DEBUG] Review Content for FrontendDeveloper -> SystemArchitect:
  [architecture.md] # ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document  ---  ## Section 1: Backend System Design  ### 1.1 Flask Application Structure  The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:  ``` /content_publishing_hub   /app     /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area     /services          # Business logic and processing services     /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions     /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)     /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic     /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed     /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)     __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints   /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)   config.py            # Configuration settings   run.py               # Application entry point   requirements.txt     # Python dependencies ```  ### 1.2 Module Responsibilities  - **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.  - **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.  - **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.  - **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.  - **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.  - **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.  ### 1.3 Data File Access and Management  - All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory. - The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data. - Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption. - Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications. - Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.  ### 1.4 Data Flow  - User requests hit Flask routes (controllers). - Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods. - Service methods utilize models to load and update data files. - Version control service manages version and approval related workflows. - Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering. - For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files. - For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.  ---  ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints  | Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes | |-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------| | /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard | /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history | /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status | /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles | /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view | /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary  ### Routing Details  - Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed. - GET routes primarily fetch and display data. - POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions. - Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering. - Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.  ---  ## Section 3: Version Control Design  ### 3.1 Architecture Overview  - Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID. - Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary. - Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps. - Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion. - Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.  ### 3.2 Data Relationships  - `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`. - `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version. - `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback. - `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.  ### 3.3 Versioning Workflow  - When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number. - Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow. - Comments can be added during review for each version. - Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary. - Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.  ### 3.4 Storage and Access  - Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions. - Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.  ---  ## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points  ### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates  - Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications. - Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values. - Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.  ### 4.2 Endpoint Responses  - GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data. - POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.  ### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend  - Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs. - Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering. - Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.  ---  This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.

# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Design Document

---

## Section 1: Backend System Design

### 1.1 Flask Application Structure

The Flask backend application will be organized into a modular package structure to separate concerns clearly and facilitate maintainability:

```
/content_publishing_hub
  /app
    /routes            # Route handlers (controllers) for each app area
    /services          # Business logic and processing services
    /models            # Data access and manipulation abstractions
    /utils             # Utility functions (file IO, helpers)
    /version_control   # Versioning and approval workflow logic
    /auth              # Authentication and session management if needed
    /templates         # HTML template files (frontend integration)
    __init__.py        # Initializes Flask app and registers blueprints
  /data                # Raw data text files (articles.txt, approvals.txt, etc.)
  config.py            # Configuration settings
  run.py               # Application entry point
  requirements.txt     # Python dependencies
```

### 1.2 Module Responsibilities

- **routes**: Defines all Flask route functions corresponding to URL endpoints. Routes handle HTTP requests, parse inputs, invoke service layer, and return rendered templates or JSON.

- **services**: Encapsulates core business logic such as article creation, editing, versioning, approval processing, and analytics summarization. Services operate on data models and help keep routes lean.

- **models**: Interacts directly with the underlying data files (e.g., articles.txt, comments.txt). Implements loading, parsing, querying, updating, and saving text file data with appropriate locking or synchronization.

- **utils**: Provides helper functions for file reading/writing, date formatting, data validation, and any other shared utility.

- **version_control**: Dedicated to managing article version history, approvals, comments, and workflow stages. Coordinates with models to persist versioning data.

- **auth**: Manages user session handling and authentication (extendable). Currently scoped for session management of logged-in users.

### 1.3 Data File Access and Management

- All persistent data stored as plain text files under `/data` directory.
- The `models` layer abstracts the file format specifics and offers programmatic access to data.
- Read/write methods use appropriate file locking or atomic writes to avoid data corruption.
- Loading data into memory for querying and saving back after modifications.
- Data integrity is critical, especially for articles and versioning; thus, service layer enforces validation and consistency.

### 1.4 Data Flow

- User requests hit Flask routes (controllers).
- Routes validate inputs and invoke corresponding service methods.
- Service methods utilize models to load and update data files.
- Version control service manages version and approval related workflows.
- Responses packaged with context variables and passed to frontend templates for rendering.
- For forms (POST), data flows from frontend to route, then service, and finally models to update files.
- For GET requests, data is gathered from models, processed by services, and sent to templates.

---

## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints

| Route | Methods | Controller Function | Input Parameters | Output / Template | Notes |
|-----------------------------|---------|-----------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|--------|
| /dashboard | GET | dashboard | session user info | dashboard.html with user stats, activity | Displays personalized dashboard
| /article/create | GET, POST | create_article | POST: form data (title, content, etc.) | create_article.html or redirect | Creation form and submission
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/edit | GET, POST | edit_article | article_id (dynamic), POST form data | edit_article.html with article data | Edit article and save versions
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/versions | GET | article_version_history | article_id | version_history.html with version list | View article version history
| /articles/mine | GET | my_articles | session username, optional filters | my_articles.html with user articles | Filters by user and status
| /articles/published | GET | published_articles | optional filter_category, sort_by | published_articles.html with published list | List published articles
| /calendar | GET | content_calendar | optional view selector | content_calendar.html with schedule data | Content calendar view
| /article/&lt;article_id&gt;/analytics | GET | article_analytics | article_id | article_analytics.html with stats | Shows analytics summary

### Routing Details

- Dynamic parameters like `article_id` passed via URL segment and validated to int or string as needed.
- GET routes primarily fetch and display data.
- POST routes process form submissions for create/edit actions.
- Session data used to capture logged-in username for personalized data filtering.
- Authentication layers (if added) will guard sensitive routes.

---

## Section 3: Version Control Design

### 3.1 Architecture Overview

- Article versions are managed as sequential numbered versions linked to a core article ID.
- Each version stores full content, author, timestamp, and change summary.
- Approval records track reviewer decisions per version including status, comments, and timestamps.
- Comments are linked to article versions allowing contextual discussion.
- Workflow stages define required approvals per article category.

### 3.2 Data Relationships

- `article_versions.txt` links by `article_id` with multiple versions distinguished by `version_number`.
- `approvals.txt` references `article_id` and `version_id` to track approval status per version.
- `comments.txt` similarly linked per article and version for ongoing feedback.
- `workflow_stages.txt` defines pipeline stages per article category affecting approval requirements.

### 3.3 Versioning Workflow

- When an article is edited and saved as new version, a new version entry is appended with incremented version_number.
- Approvers can mark versions as approved, rejected, or request revisions via the approval workflow.
- Comments can be added during review for each version.
- Version history pages query and display all versions and their approval summary.
- Restoration of previous versions involves copying content from a selected version to create a new draft version.

### 3.4 Storage and Access

- Version control logic accesses respective data files through model abstractions.
- Updates to versions, approvals, and comments are persisted atomically to respective text files.

---

## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points

### 4.1 Data Passing to Templates

- Each route renders templates with context variables matching design_spec.md specifications.
- Data such as username, article lists, version details, analytics summaries are passed as dicts, lists, or scalar values.
- Variables follow clear naming conventions e.g., `article_id`, `versions`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity`.

### 4.2 Endpoint Responses

- GET endpoints render full HTML pages populated with context data.
- POST endpoints typically redirect post-processing or return validation messages within templates.

### 4.3 Coordination with Frontend

- Frontend teams will consume context variables to populate page elements identified by specified IDs.
- Careful coordination on data structures, e.g., list of dicts for articles and versions, is necessary to ensure correct rendering.
- Navigation actions mapped to routes should be consistent with backend URL structure.

---

This architecture document provides the comprehensive backend design, routing logic, version control strategy, and frontend integration approach to enable independent development and integration of the ContentPublishingHub system.
